September · Infant

All About Me & My Family  ·  Letter Ss
MONTH September
THEME All About Me & My Family
LETTER Ss
Number 2 · Shape square · Color orange
Teacher: _______________Classroom: _______________Week of: _______________Take-home: The Home Den family pack

Focus — secure attachment, face-to-face “serve & return,” and a sign of the month

Sign of the Month

  • “More” (and “all done”) — model at every feeding.
  • Bonus family sign: “mama / dada.”
  • Narrate each baby by name; echo coos and add one word.

Songs & Lap Play

  • “Where Is Baby?” (peekaboo with a scarf)
  • “This Little Piggy”
  • Name-sung hellos: “Hel-lo, baby ___.”

Sensory Picks

  • Non-breakable floor mirror
  • High-contrast family photo cards
  • Peekaboo scarves
  • Soft crinkle books
FLORIDA EARLY LEARNING STANDARDS — DOMAINS ADDRESSED
Physical DevelopmentApproaches to LearningSocial & Emotional DevelopmentLanguage & LiteracyScientific InquiryCreative Expression
Milestones this band builds toward: secure attachment & trust; exploring with the senses and reaching, grasping & grabbing; responding to voices, babbling & first sounds; and gaining head, trunk & hand control.
Aligned to the Florida Early Learning and Developmental Standards: Birth to Kindergarten (2017), FDOE Division of Early Learning. Domain alignments are paraphrased teaching summaries, not the official standards text. See the standards by age in our Milestone Wizard →

  • Play the Bear Phonics Alphabet Anthem from Mrs. Bear’s Welcome to Success! album — the ABCs in a song. Play on YouTube →

Your Feelings Matter

  • A laminated feelings-faces card at the diaper station — name your own face: “Teacher is happy to see you!”
  • Get the Your Feelings Matter book →

The Home Den — the family take-home pack

Goes in every backpack this month.

  • Family photo card to laminate for the crib area.
  • A “sign ‘more’ with me” half-sheet for parents.
  • A lullaby list for the car and bedtime.
  • One “serve-and-return” tip card.

Infants get the take-home pack + a sign-language focus instead of a weekly grid.

The printable Home Den pack for this month — mini-book, practice pages & cover sheet — is available to The Buzz monthly subscribers.

Join The Buzz →

Snuggle up and share a read-aloud — try Your Feelings Matter or a favorite picture book.

Book list: Bear Phonics See Me & See Me Eat Meat (watch on Bear Phonics) · Your Feelings Matter — “I belong / I’m proud of me” (get on Amazon) · suggested trade books on family & feelings (teacher’s choice).

Song & fingerplay sheet: “Twinkle, Twinkle” · “If You’re Happy…” · “The More We Get Together”.

Materials shopping list — tap any item to shop on Amazon: Non-breakable floor mirror · high-contrast family photo cards · peekaboo scarves · soft crinkle & cloth books · duplicate soft loveys.

Printables: fill-in weekly grid · “All About Me” mini-book · family-portrait frame · Ss / number-2 / square practice page · the September Home Den cover sheet · “See the Work” Friday checklist.

Weekly Plan — four sub-themes across the developmental domains

Week · Sub-themePhysicalLanguage / LiteracySocial-EmotionalSensory / Explore
Week 1
This Is Me		Mirror play — pat your nose, headName each body part in a songPoint to own photo, smile backFace-parts felt board
Week 2
My Family		Carry a “baby” doll to the cribFamily photo book, name facesHug the doll, pat gentlyFabric squares = “family blankets”
Week 3
My Feelings		Big / soft movements to a feeling song“Happy face / sad face” board bookAdult names the feeling in the momentCalm-down basket introduced
Week 4
My Friends		Roll a ball to a friend“Bye-bye” wave song at pickupParallel play, two of each toyBubble “hello” at the door

Physical DevelopmentApproaches to LearningSocial & Emotional DevelopmentLanguage & LiteracyScientific InquiryCreative Expression

Number 2 · Shape square · Color orange
Teacher: _______________Classroom: _______________Week of: _______________Take-home: The Home Den family pack

Weekly Plan — four sub-themes across the developmental domains

Week · Sub-themePhysicalLanguage / LiteracyMath / ScienceSocial-EmotionalCreative
Week 1
This Is Me		“Head, Shoulders, Knees & Toes”Name-card photo hunt; “I am ___”Count 2 eyes, 2 hands (number 2)Self-portrait mirror lookPaint a “me” paper-plate face
Week 2
My Family		Push a stroller / doll around the roomFamily photo wall; who is this?Sort big / little family shoesRock & feed the baby dollFamily collage with photos
Week 3
My Feelings		Stomp when mad, float when calmFeelings picture cards + mirrorMatch happy / sad faces (sorting)Practice “breathe like bubbles”Play-dough feeling faces
Week 4
My Friends		Roll / toss ball naming a friend“My friend is ___” at circleCount friends at the tableTake turns with a sand timerHandprint “friendship tree”

Physical DevelopmentApproaches to LearningLanguage & LiteracyMathematical ThinkingScientific InquirySocial & Emotional DevelopmentCreative Expression
Milestones this band builds toward: running, jumping & scribbling; speaking in 2–3 word phrases; sorting & matching by one attribute; symbolic and parallel play; and growing self-help skills.

Number 2 · Shape square · Color orange
Teacher: _______________Classroom: _______________Week of: _______________Take-home: The Home Den family pack

Weekly Plan — four sub-themes across the developmental domains

Week · Sub-themePhysicalLanguage / LiteracyMathScienceSocial-EmotionalCreative
Week 1
This Is Me		Body trace on big paperName card: find, trace, stampCount body parts to 105 senses: taste / smell / touch table“I am special because…”Life-size self-portrait
Week 2
My Family		Act out family jobs (sweep, cook)Draw & label “my family”; dictateSort family by size (tall / short)How families are alike / differentFamily roles & belongingFamily photo picture-frame craft
Week 3
My Feelings		Feeling freeze-dance (mad / happy / calm)Feelings book read-aloud + retellGraph “how we feel today”Why does my heart beat fast?Name feelings + causes; empathyFeelings faces watercolor
Week 4
My Friends		Cooperative parachute / ball games“A friend is someone who…” chartCount & compare friends per centerSink / float: our favorite toysTurn-taking, kind wordsHandprint friendship wreath
FLORIDA EARLY LEARNING STANDARDS — DOMAINS ADDRESSED
Physical DevelopmentApproaches to LearningLanguage & LiteracyMathematical ThinkingScientific InquirySocial & Emotional DevelopmentCreative Expression
Milestones this band builds toward: speaking in sentences & asking questions; counting and knowing some numbers, shapes, colors & letters; drawing basic shapes; beginning cooperative play & turn-taking; and growing self-regulation.
Aligned to the Florida Early Learning and Developmental Standards: Birth to Kindergarten (2017), FDOE Division of Early Learning. Domain alignments are paraphrased teaching summaries, not the official standards text. See the standards by age in our Milestone Wizard →

September · Fours (Pre-K / VPK)

All About Me & My Family  ·  Letter Ss
MONTH September
THEME All About Me & My Family
LETTER Ss
Number 2 · Shape square · Color orange
Teacher: _______________Classroom: _______________Week of: _______________Take-home: The Home Den family pack

The lead band. The Marva-rhythm daily block folds Bear Phonics in as the literacy core.

Weekly Plan — four sub-themes across the developmental domains

Week · Sub-themePhysicalLanguage & LiteracyMathScienceSocial StudiesSocial-EmotionalCreative
Week 1
This Is Me		Trace body; write my nameSs intro; name in print; “All About Me” bookCount 1-to-1 to 5; number 2; pairs5 senses investigation stationsI am part of a family & a class“I am proud that I can…”Self-portrait with mirror
Week 2
My Family		Fine-motor: family finger puppetsDraw + dictate a family story; family wordsSort / graph family members; more / fewerAlike & different among familiesFamily roles, homes, culturesBelonging; my job in the familyFamily portrait, labeled
Week 3
My Feelings		Yoga: calm-down “smell the flower”Feelings vocabulary; read-aloud + retellFeelings graph; count & compareBody clues: how feelings feelHow we help friends feel betterName feelings + causes; empathyFeelings self-portrait series
Week 4
My Friends & My Class		Cooperative team gamesClass-made “Our Den” friendship bookPattern with friends (AB); count classSink / float with class toys (predict)Class rules we make togetherTurn-taking, solving small conflictsMural: “This Is Our Class”
FLORIDA EARLY LEARNING STANDARDS — DOMAINS ADDRESSED
Physical DevelopmentApproaches to LearningSocial & Emotional DevelopmentLanguage & LiteracyMathematical ThinkingScientific InquirySocial StudiesCreative Expression
Milestones this band builds toward: writing their name & knowing many letter-sounds; counting to 20 & making patterns; retelling stories with emergent writing; solving problems and cooperating in groups; and self-regulating — VPK / kindergarten ready.
Aligned to the Florida Early Learning and Developmental Standards: Birth to Kindergarten (2017), FDOE Division of Early Learning. Domain alignments are paraphrased teaching summaries, not the official standards text. See the standards by age in our Milestone Wizard →

Bear Phonics

  • Warm-up: Sound Clock S, then T. Teach: read “See Me” (Lesson 1), Socratic questions.
  • Workbook (you-do): Bear Tracks Lesson 1 — Meet S, Write S, find-the-S grid; then Lesson 2 “See Me Eat Meat” (t).
  • Apply: re-read the decodable; Friday mastery check + “I did it!” win.
  • Watch Lessons 1–2 free on Bear Phonics →

Your Feelings Matter

  • Feelings check-in chart every morning.
  • Read the Your Feelings Matter “I belong / I’m proud of me” title; build the class kindness tree.
  • Role-play “how can we help ___ feel better?”
  • Get the book →

Books & Read-Alouds

  • Your Feelings Matter — “I belong / I’m proud of me” title. Get on Amazon →
  • Bear Phonics “See Me” & “See Me Eat Meat” decodable readers. Watch on Bear Phonics →
  • Diverse family & “all about me” picture books (teacher’s choice).
Browse the Reading Library →

September · School Age

All About Me & My Family  ·  Letter Ss
MONTH September
THEME All About Me & My Family
LETTER Ss
Number 2 · Shape square · Color orange
Teacher: _______________Classroom: _______________Week of: _______________Take-home: The Home Den family pack

Before / after care — projects, journaling, and leadership, not circle time.

Weekly Plan — four sub-themes across the developmental domains

Week · Sub-themeFocusActivity
Week 1
This Is Me		Identity & goals“About Me” journal page + a personal goal for the year; interview a partner
Week 2
My Family		Family & heritageFamily tree or “my family map”; share a family tradition or recipe
Week 3
My Feelings		SEL & self-regulationFeelings journal; make a personal “calm-down toolkit”; discuss what helps
Week 4
My Friends & Community		Belonging & leadershipDesign “our after-school code”; be a reading buddy to a younger class
FLORIDA EARLY LEARNING STANDARDS — DOMAINS ADDRESSED
Approaches to LearningSocial & Emotional DevelopmentLanguage & LiteracyMathematical ThinkingScientific InquirySocial StudiesCreative Expression
Milestones this band builds toward: reading & writing with growing independence; adding and subtracting; leading projects and working in teams; setting goals and self-directing; and expressing ideas across the arts.
Aligned to the Florida Early Learning and Developmental Standards: Birth to Kindergarten (2017), FDOE Division of Early Learning. Domain alignments are paraphrased teaching summaries, not the official standards text. See the standards by age in our Milestone Wizard →

Bear Phonics

  • Leadership tie-in: School Agers become reading buddies — they read “See Me” aloud to the Twos / Threes.
  • Great confidence builder + drives familiarity with the readers.
  • Watch on Bear Phonics →

  • Older-kid feelings journal + personal “calm-down toolkit.”
  • Talk through what belonging means.

The Home Den 🐾 Family Handout

September · Infant

All About Me & My Family · a note to take home

Baby’s biggest lesson this month is you. Faces, names, and cuddles are how little ones first learn: “I belong.”

Letter SsNumber 2Shape: squareColor: orangeTheme: All About Me & My Family

Try this at home

  • Play peekaboo with a scarf.
  • Sign “more” at every feeding.
  • Name faces in a family photo.
  • Talk, then pause — let baby “answer” with coos.

Sing together

  • “This Little Piggy”
  • “Where Is Baby?” (peekaboo)

Read together

Snuggle up and share a read-aloud together — try Your Feelings Matter or a favorite picture book. Decodable Bear Phonics readers begin at age three.

September · Ones

All About Me & My Family · a note to take home

Your one-year-old is discovering “me” and “my family.” Name everything in sight — it grows their words fast.

Letter SsNumber 2Shape: squareColor: orangeTheme: All About Me & My Family

Try this at home

  • Name body parts at bath time.
  • Look at a family photo book together.
  • Make the “sssss” snake sound.
  • Point to happy and sad faces.

Sing together

  • “Where Is Thumbkin?”
  • “If You’re Happy and You Know It”

Read together

Snuggle up and share a read-aloud together — try Your Feelings Matter or a favorite picture book. Decodable Bear Phonics readers begin at age three.

September · Twos

All About Me & My Family · a note to take home

Twos love to say “me!” and “mine!” Lean in — this month is all about who they are and who loves them.

Letter SsNumber 2Shape: squareColor: orangeTheme: All About Me & My Family

Try this at home

  • Make a paper-plate “me” face.
  • Hunt for things that start with sss.
  • Count 2 eyes, 2 hands, 2 shoes.
  • Name a feeling out loud together.

Sing together

  • “Twinkle, Twinkle” (S is for star!)
  • “The More We Get Together”

Read together

Snuggle up and share a read-aloud together — try Your Feelings Matter or a favorite picture book. Decodable Bear Phonics readers begin at age three.

September · Threes

All About Me & My Family · a note to take home

Threes are ready to tell you all about themselves. Ask lots of “who” and “why,” and listen big.

Letter SsNumber 2Shape: squareColor: orangeTheme: All About Me & My Family

Try this at home

  • Draw “my family” and label who’s who.
  • Practice writing the letter S.
  • Count to 2 and find squares around the house.
  • Talk about a feeling — and what caused it.

Sing together

  • “This Is My Family”
  • “If You’re Happy…”

Read together

Read See Me together tonight — point to each word as you say it. It’s in this packet, and free on Bear Phonics.

September · Fours (Pre-K / VPK)

All About Me & My Family · a note to take home

Your Pre-K’er is becoming a reader! This month they meet the letter S and read their very first sentence: “See me!”

Letter SsNumber 2Shape: squareColor: orangeTheme: All About Me & My Family

Try this at home

  • Read See Me together — let them point to each word.
  • Write your child’s name together.
  • Practice S, the number 2, and squares.
  • Talk about a feeling and why it happened.

Sing together

  • “Twinkle, Twinkle” (Ss)
  • “The More We Get Together”

Read together

Let your child read See Me to you — they can do it! It’s printed in this packet, and free on Bear Phonics.

September · School Age

All About Me & My Family · a note to take home

Big kids shine as leaders and helpers this month. Invite them to teach what they know.

Letter SsNumber 2Shape: squareColor: orangeTheme: All About Me & My Family

Try this at home

  • Share a family tradition or recipe.
  • Read See Me aloud to a younger sibling.
  • Start an “About Me” journal page.
  • Plan a family game night together.

Do together

  • Family game night
  • “Success Anthem” warm-up

Read together

Have them read See Me as a reading buddy — teaching is the best way to master it. It’s in this packet, and free on Bear Phonics.

October Decodable Reader

“See Me Eat Meat!” · Bear Phonics Lesson 2

October’s reader adds the new sound T (review M · E · S) — blending all the way to a whole sentence: “See me eat meat.”

Read it together, then watch it free on Bear Phonics on YouTube. The full printed book is available separately.

October · Infant

The Great Outdoors  ·  Letters T · G · J
MONTH October
THEME The Great Outdoors
LETTERS T · G · J
Number 3 · Shape triangle · Color brown
Teacher: _______________Classroom: _______________Week of: _______________Take-home: The Home Den family pack

Focus — outdoor senses, gentle movement, and one new sound (T)

Sound & Sensory

  • Listen for birds and wind on a stroller walk; name what you hear.
  • Bear Phonics /t/ — the “tick-tock” clock sound; tap a toy clock.
  • Touch a smooth leaf and a crinkly leaf (always supervised).

Songs & Lap Play

  • “The Leaves Are Falling” (float a scarf down)
  • “Twinkle, Twinkle” (night sky)
  • Name-sung hellos: “Hel-lo, baby ___.”

Nature Sensory Picks

  • Non-breakable floor mirror
  • Big leaves & pinecones (supervised)
  • Nature texture board
  • Soft animal toys
FLORIDA EARLY LEARNING STANDARDS — DOMAINS ADDRESSED
Physical DevelopmentApproaches to LearningSocial & Emotional DevelopmentLanguage & LiteracyScientific InquiryCreative Expression
Milestones this band builds toward: secure attachment & trust; exploring with the senses and reaching, grasping & grabbing; responding to voices, babbling & first sounds; and gaining head, trunk & hand control.
Aligned to the Florida Early Learning and Developmental Standards: Birth to Kindergarten (2017), FDOE Division of Early Learning. Domain alignments are paraphrased teaching summaries, not the official standards text. See the standards by age in our Milestone Wizard →

Bear Phonics

  • Play the Bear Phonics Alphabet Anthem from Mrs. Bear’s Welcome to Success! album — the ABCs in a song. Play on YouTube →

Your Feelings Matter

  • A laminated feelings-faces card outside — “the wind feels silly!”
  • Get the Your Feelings Matter book →

Books & Read-Alouds

  • Your Feelings Matter by Mrs. Bear — name feelings together. Get on Amazon →
  • We’re Going on a Leaf Hunt by Steve Metzger
  • The Little Yellow Leaf by Carin Berger
Browse the Reading Library →

Character Development — Responsibility

  • Model gentle care: “We are soft with our friends and our things.”
  • Narrate clean-up as you tidy: “Teacher puts the toy away.”

ECE Fun Fact — for teachers

Outdoor play isn’t a break from learning — it is learning. Children with daily outdoor time show sharper focus, stronger motor skills, and lower stress; even 20 minutes of “green time” boosts attention. Take a lesson outside this week!

Bear Phonics

  • Warm-up: Sound Clock M / E / S, then new T. Teach: read “See Me Eat Meat” (Lesson 2).
  • Workbook: Bear Tracks Lesson 2 — Meet T, Write T, find-the-T grid.
  • Apply: re-read the decodable; Friday mastery check + “I did it!”.
  • Watch Lessons 1–2 free on Bear Phonics →

  • Feelings check-in every morning.
  • Build the class kindness tree; role-play helping.

ECE Fun Fact — for teachers

Outdoor play isn’t a break from learning — it is learning. Children with daily outdoor time show sharper focus, stronger motor skills, and lower stress; even 20 minutes of “green time” boosts attention. Take a lesson outside this week!

October · Infant

The Great Outdoors · a note to take home

Autumn is a feast for the senses. Bundle up and let baby feel the wind, hear the birds, and touch a leaf — that’s real learning.

Letters T · G · JNumber 3Shape: triangleColor: brownTheme: The Great Outdoors

Try this at home

  • Go on a “listen for the birds” walk.
  • Let baby touch a smooth and a crinkly leaf (watch closely).
  • Make the /t/ “tick-tock” clock sound.
  • Point to the sun, a tree, a bird.

Sing together

  • “The Leaves Are Falling”
  • “Twinkle, Twinkle”

Read together

Snuggle up and share a read-aloud together — try Your Feelings Matter or a favorite picture book. Decodable Bear Phonics readers begin at age three.
The Preschool Professional · Built with love by Mrs. Bear · Free to use, no strings.

October · Ones

The Great Outdoors · a note to take home

Your one-year-old is a little explorer! Every leaf, bug, and puddle is a lesson. Get outside and name what you see.

Letters T · G · JNumber 3Shape: triangleColor: brownTheme: The Great Outdoors

Try this at home

  • Collect 3 leaves on a walk.
  • Find something that starts with /t/ (tree, toy).
  • Watch a bug together — be gentle.
  • Talk about today’s weather at the window.

Sing together

  • “The Leaves on the Trees”
  • “If You’re Happy and You Know It”

Read together

Snuggle up and share a read-aloud together — try Your Feelings Matter or a favorite picture book. Decodable Bear Phonics readers begin at age three.

October · Twos

The Great Outdoors · a note to take home

Twos love to dig, stomp, and discover. This month we’re outside — leaves, bugs, weather, and animal homes!

Letters T · G · JNumber 3Shape: triangleColor: brownTheme: The Great Outdoors

Try this at home

  • Make a leaf rubbing with a crayon.
  • Go on a backyard bug hunt.
  • Count 3 rocks, 3 leaves, 3 sticks.
  • Say the /t/ sound and trace the letter T.

Sing together

  • “The Leaves Are Falling Down”
  • “Itsy Bitsy Spider”

Read together

Snuggle up and share a read-aloud together — try Your Feelings Matter or a favorite picture book. Decodable Bear Phonics readers begin at age three.

October · Threes

The Great Outdoors · a note to take home

Threes are full of “why?” Nature gives you a hundred answers. Explore the outdoors together and wonder out loud.

Letters T · G · JNumber 3Shape: triangleColor: brownTheme: The Great Outdoors

Try this at home

  • Do a nature scavenger hunt.
  • Draw “my backyard” and label it.
  • Sort leaves big / little and count to 3.
  • Read See Me Eat Meat and practice writing T.

Sing together

  • “Autumn Leaves Are Falling”
  • “This Is the Way We Rake the Leaves”

Read together

Read See Me Eat Meat tonight — point to each word. It’s printed in this packet, and free on Bear Phonics.

October · Fours (Pre-K / VPK)

The Great Outdoors · a note to take home

Your Pre-K’er is reading more every week! This month they add the T sound and read a whole sentence: “See me eat meat.”

Letters T · G · JNumber 3Shape: triangleColor: brownTheme: The Great Outdoors

Try this at home

  • Start a “My Nature Journal” — collect & label 3 finds.
  • Read See Me Eat Meat together.
  • Practice letters T, G, J and the number 3.
  • Give your child a job at home — responsibility grows big kids.

Sing together

  • “Five Little Leaves”
  • “Itsy Bitsy Spider”

Read together

Let your child read See Me Eat Meat to you. It’s printed in this packet, and free on Bear Phonics.

Focus — sensory play, gentle movement, and one new sound

Sound & Sensory

  • Coo back and forth with “thankful” happy faces.
  • Bear Phonics /h/ listening — “ha-ha!”
  • Warm textures: soft blankets.

Songs & Lap Play

  • “I’m Thankful”
  • “This Little Piggy”
  • Gentle rocking songs

Sensory Picks

  • Autumn-leaf photo cards
  • Soft pumpkins
  • Family photos
  • Warm fuzzy fabrics

Character Development — Gratitude

  • Say “thank you” at snack and clean-up.
  • Notice one good thing together each day.

ECE Fun Fact — for teachers

Gratitude is teachable! Children who practice naming what they’re thankful for show a more positive mood and better sleep. A daily “one good thing” circle builds the habit.

November · Fours (Pre-K / VPK)

Thankful Hearts  ·  Letters H · K · L
MONTH November
THEME Thankful Hearts
LETTERS H · K · L
Number 4 · Shape rectangle · Color yellow
Teacher: _______________Classroom: _______________Week of: _______________Take-home: The Home Den family pack

The lead band. The Marva-rhythm daily block folds Bear Phonics in as the literacy core.

Weekly Plan — four sub-themes across the developmental domains

Week · Sub-themePhysicalLanguage & LiteracyMathScienceSocial StudiesSocial-EmotionalCreative
Week 1
I Am Thankful		Gratitude yoga stretches“I am thankful for…”Count our blessings to 4Five senses to be thankful forThankful for people who help usName a happy feelingThankful-tree handprint leaves
Week 2
Family & Home		Act out family choresDraw & tell about my familyCount family membersHomes keep us warm & safeFamilies are all differentI belong in my familyFamily portrait
Week 3
Sharing & Giving		Pass-it-along movement game“Please & thank you” practiceShare snacks equallyHow helping feels goodPeople who give in our communityTake turns & shareMake a thank-you card
Week 4
A Thankful Feast		Set the table; carry with careName harvest foods (H sound!)Count plates & cupsWhere our food comes fromFeasts & gratitude traditionsGratitude circlePaper-plate harvest craft
FLORIDA EARLY LEARNING STANDARDS — DOMAINS ADDRESSED
Physical DevelopmentApproaches to LearningSocial & Emotional DevelopmentLanguage & LiteracyMathematical ThinkingScientific InquirySocial StudiesCreative Expression
Milestones this band builds toward: writing their name & knowing many letter-sounds; counting to 20 & making patterns; retelling stories with emergent writing; solving problems and cooperating in groups; and self-regulating — VPK / kindergarten ready.
Aligned to the Florida Early Learning and Developmental Standards: Birth to Kindergarten (2017), FDOE Division of Early Learning. Domain alignments are paraphrased teaching summaries, not the official standards text. See the standards by age in our Milestone Wizard →

Bear Phonics

  • Warm-up: Sound Clock review, then new H. Teach: read “He Eats Meat” (Lesson 3).
  • Workbook: Bear Tracks Lesson 3 — Meet H, Write H.
  • Apply: re-read the decodable; Friday mastery check + “I did it!”.
  • Watch Lesson 3 free on Bear Phonics →

Your Feelings Matter

  • Feelings check-in every morning.
  • Name feelings + causes; role-play helping.
  • Get the book →

Books & Read-Alouds

  • Your Feelings Matter. Get on Amazon →
  • Bear Phonics “He Eats Meat” decodable reader. Watch on Bear Phonics →
  • Bear Says Thanks by Karma Wilson
  • Thank You, Omu! by Oge Mora
Browse the Reading Library →

Character Development — Gratitude

  • Keep a class gratitude chart — add one thing daily.
  • Draw or write thank-you notes to a helper.

ECE Fun Fact — for teachers

Gratitude is teachable! Children who practice naming what they’re thankful for show a more positive mood and better sleep. A daily “one good thing” circle builds the habit.

Music & Movement from Mrs. Bear’s “Welcome to Success!” album

One tap plays the track. The Success Anthem is the recurring phonics anthem — use it often.

The Home Den — the family take-home pack

Goes in every backpack this month.

  • A “what I’m thankful for” drawing page.
  • A family gratitude-at-dinner card.
  • A thankful-hearts craft.
  • H / K / L + number-4 tracing.

The printable Home Den pack for this month — mini-book, practice pages & cover sheet — is available to The Buzz monthly subscribers.

Join The Buzz →

Then read this month’s Bear Phonics book together: He Eats Meat.

Songs & Fingerplays

  • “I’m Thankful” (to Frère Jacques)
  • “The More We Get Together”
  • “If You’re Happy and You Know It”

Materials — tap to shop

Thankful-tree branches · leaves for writing · family-photo frames · H/K/L tiles · harvest play food.

Shop the Center Bundles →

Teacher Resources — November (all ages)

Book list: Bear Phonics He Eats Meat (Lesson 3) (watch on Bear Phonics) · a favorite thankful hearts picture book (teacher’s choice) · Your Feelings Matter (get on Amazon).

Letters this month: H · K · L · Number 4 · rectangle · yellow.

Materials shopping list — tap any item to shop on Amazon: Thankful-tree branches · leaves for writing · family-photo frames · H/K/L tiles · harvest play food.

November · School Age

Thankful Hearts  ·  Letters H · K · L
MONTH November
THEME Thankful Hearts
LETTERS H · K · L
Number 4 · Shape rectangle · Color yellow
Teacher: _______________Classroom: _______________Week of: _______________Take-home: The Home Den family pack

Before / after care — projects, journaling, and leadership, not circle time.

Weekly Plan — four sub-themes across the developmental domains

Week · Sub-themeFocusActivity
Week 1
I Am Thankful		GratitudeKeep a gratitude journal; a “thankful for” wall
Week 2
Family & Home		Family & heritageShare a family recipe or story
Week 3
Sharing & Giving		ServicePlan a class giving / thank-you project
Week 4
A Thankful Feast		ReflectionWrite thank-you notes to school helpers
FLORIDA EARLY LEARNING STANDARDS — DOMAINS ADDRESSED
Approaches to LearningSocial & Emotional DevelopmentLanguage & LiteracyMathematical ThinkingScientific InquirySocial StudiesCreative Expression
Milestones this band builds toward: reading & writing with growing independence; adding and subtracting; leading projects and working in teams; setting goals and self-directing; and expressing ideas across the arts.
Aligned to the Florida Early Learning and Developmental Standards: Birth to Kindergarten (2017), FDOE Division of Early Learning. Domain alignments are paraphrased teaching summaries, not the official standards text. See the standards by age in our Milestone Wizard →

Bear Phonics

  • Leadership tie-in: read “He Eats Meat” aloud to the Twos / Threes.
  • Challenge: build new /h/ words on the word wall.
  • Watch on Bear Phonics →

Your Feelings Matter

  • Older-kid feelings journal + a personal “calm-down toolkit.”
  • Get the Your Feelings Matter book →

November · Infant

Thankful Hearts · a note to take home

This month our hearts are full. Practice gratitude together — name one good thing at dinner. Thankfulness grows happy, healthy kids.

Letters H · K · LNumber 4Shape: rectangleColor: yellowTheme: Thankful Hearts

Try this at home

  • A “what I’m thankful for” drawing page.
  • A family gratitude-at-dinner card.
  • A thankful-hearts craft.
  • H / K / L + number-4 tracing.

Sing together

  • “I’m Thankful” (to Frère Jacques)
  • “The More We Get Together”

Read together

Snuggle up and share a read-aloud together — try Your Feelings Matter or a favorite picture book. Decodable Bear Phonics readers begin at age three.

December Decodable Reader

Read it together, then watch it free on Bear Phonics on YouTube. The full printed book is available separately.

December · Infant

Lights & Traditions Around the World  ·  Letters W · F · N · O
MONTH December
THEME Lights & Traditions Around the World
LETTERS W · F · N · O
Number 5 · Shape star · Color green
Teacher: _______________Classroom: _______________Week of: _______________Take-home: The Home Den family pack

Focus — sensory play, gentle movement, and one new sound

Sound & Sensory

  • Watch soft twinkle lights (supervised).
  • Bear Phonics /w/ /f/ sounds at play.
  • Textured ornaments to touch.

Songs & Lap Play

  • “Twinkle, Twinkle”
  • “This Little Light of Mine”
  • Lullabies from many cultures

Sensory Picks

  • Safe shiny / crinkly items
  • Battery tea-lights (supervised)
  • Soft star toys
  • Family photos
FLORIDA EARLY LEARNING STANDARDS — DOMAINS ADDRESSED
Physical DevelopmentApproaches to LearningSocial & Emotional DevelopmentLanguage & LiteracyScientific InquiryCreative Expression
Milestones this band builds toward: secure attachment & trust; exploring with the senses and reaching, grasping & grabbing; responding to voices, babbling & first sounds; and gaining head, trunk & hand control.
Aligned to the Florida Early Learning and Developmental Standards: Birth to Kindergarten (2017), FDOE Division of Early Learning. Domain alignments are paraphrased teaching summaries, not the official standards text. See the standards by age in our Milestone Wizard →

Bear Phonics

  • Play the Bear Phonics Alphabet Anthem from Mrs. Bear’s Welcome to Success! album — the ABCs in a song. Play on YouTube →

Your Feelings Matter

  • A laminated feelings-faces card nearby — name your own face: “Teacher feels happy!”
  • Get the Your Feelings Matter book →

Books & Read-Alouds

  • Your Feelings Matter by Mrs. Bear — name feelings together. Get on Amazon →
  • Celebrations Around the World by DK Children
  • The Shortest Day by Susan Cooper
Browse the Reading Library →

Character Development — Generosity

  • Share a toy: “your turn, my turn.”
  • Give a warm “here you go!”

ECE Fun Fact — for teachers

Exposure to many cultures and traditions in early childhood builds cognitive flexibility — the brain’s ability to shift perspectives. Celebrate broadly!

The Home Den — the family take-home pack

Goes in every backpack this month.

  • A “family traditions” share card.
  • A paper-lantern or star craft.
  • A giving / kindness idea list.
  • W / F / N / O + number-5 tracing.

Infants get the take-home pack + a sensory focus instead of a weekly grid.

The printable Home Den pack for this month — mini-book, practice pages & cover sheet — is available to The Buzz monthly subscribers.

Snuggle up and share a read-aloud — try Your Feelings Matter or a favorite picture book.

Teacher Resources — December (all ages)

Book list: Bear Phonics We See Feet (Lesson 4) (watch on Bear Phonics) · a favorite lights & traditions around the world picture book (teacher’s choice) · Your Feelings Matter (get on Amazon).

Letters this month: W · F · N · O · Number 5 · star · green.

Printables: themed activity pages · letter & number practice · the December Home Den cover sheet · “See the Work” Friday checklist.

January · Infant

Winter Wonders  ·  Letters D · P · Q
MONTH January
THEME Winter Wonders
LETTERS D · P · Q
Number 6 · Shape diamond · Color blue
Teacher: _______________Classroom: _______________Week of: _______________Take-home: The Home Den family pack

Focus — sensory play, gentle movement, and one new sound

Sound & Sensory

  • Feel something cold, then warm (supervised).
  • Bear Phonics /d/ sound at play.
  • Cozy blanket textures.

Songs & Lap Play

  • “Snowflake, Snowflake”
  • “Twinkle, Twinkle”
  • Warm rocking lullabies

Sensory Picks

  • Cotton-ball “snow” (supervised)
  • White soft toys
  • Mirror
  • Cozy fabrics
FLORIDA EARLY LEARNING STANDARDS — DOMAINS ADDRESSED
Physical DevelopmentApproaches to LearningSocial & Emotional DevelopmentLanguage & LiteracyScientific InquiryCreative Expression
Milestones this band builds toward: secure attachment & trust; exploring with the senses and reaching, grasping & grabbing; responding to voices, babbling & first sounds; and gaining head, trunk & hand control.

ECE Fun Fact — for teachers

Cold weather doesn’t cause colds — but getting outside still matters. Winter outdoor play boosts vitamin D, mood, and gross-motor development. Bundle up and go!

  • A snowflake cut-out craft.
  • A “winter animals” matching card.
  • A cozy bedtime-reading tip.
  • D / P / Q + number-6 tracing.

The printable Home Den pack for this month — mini-book, practice pages & cover sheet — is available to The Buzz monthly subscribers.

Join The Buzz →

Snuggle up and share a read-aloud — try Your Feelings Matter or a favorite picture book.

January · Threes

Winter Wonders  ·  Letters D · P · Q
MONTH January
THEME Winter Wonders
LETTERS D · P · Q
Number 6 · Shape diamond · Color blue
Teacher: _______________Classroom: _______________Week of: _______________Take-home: The Home Den family pack

Weekly Plan — four sub-themes across the developmental domains

Week · Sub-themePhysicalLanguage / LiteracyMathScienceSocial-EmotionalCreative
Week 1
Snow & Ice		Ice-skating slide movementsCold words: snow, ice, frostCount snowballs to 6Ice melts: cold vs. warmCozy, calm feelingsCotton-ball snowman
Week 2
Winter Animals		Move like a bear, penguin, fox“Animals in winter” chartCount & sort animalsHibernate, migrate, adaptGentle with living thingsHandprint penguin
Week 3
Staying Warm & Cozy		Dress-for-winter relayName winter clothes (D: down, dry)Match mittens (pairs)How clothes keep us warmCozy calm-down timeDesign a mitten
Week 4
Winter Fun		Indoor “snowball” tossTell about winter playGraph favorite winter gamesWhy we see our breathShare the fun; take turnsSnowflake painting
FLORIDA EARLY LEARNING STANDARDS — DOMAINS ADDRESSED
Physical DevelopmentApproaches to LearningLanguage & LiteracyMathematical ThinkingScientific InquirySocial & Emotional DevelopmentCreative Expression
Milestones this band builds toward: speaking in sentences & asking questions; counting and knowing some numbers, shapes, colors & letters; drawing basic shapes; beginning cooperative play & turn-taking; and growing self-regulation.
Aligned to the Florida Early Learning and Developmental Standards: Birth to Kindergarten (2017), FDOE Division of Early Learning. Domain alignments are paraphrased teaching summaries, not the official standards text. See the standards by age in our Milestone Wizard →

Bear Phonics

  • Sound Clock review, then new D; read “Feed Me.”
  • “I do / we do / you do” — trace the D row (Bear Tracks).
  • Friday recite + “I did it!” Watch Lesson 5 free on Bear Phonics →

Your Feelings Matter

  • Daily feelings check-in chart.
  • Grow the class kindness tree.
  • Get the book →

Books & Read-Alouds

  • The Snowy Day by Ezra Jack Keats
  • Over and Under the Snow by Kate Messner
  • Bear Phonics “Feed Me” decodable reader. Watch on Bear Phonics →
  • Your Feelings Matter anthology. Get on Amazon →
Browse the Reading Library →

Character Development — Perseverance

  • “I haven’t got it YET” — the power of yet.
  • Set a small goal and stick with it all week.

ECE Fun Fact — for teachers

Cold weather doesn’t cause colds — but getting outside still matters. Winter outdoor play boosts vitamin D, mood, and gross-motor development. Bundle up and go!

The lead band. The Marva-rhythm daily block folds Bear Phonics in as the literacy core.

Weekly Plan — four sub-themes across the developmental domains

Week · Sub-themePhysicalLanguage & LiteracyMathScienceSocial StudiesSocial-EmotionalCreative
Week 1
Snow & Ice		Ice-skating slide movementsCold words: snow, ice, frostCount snowballs to 6Ice melts: cold vs. warmPlaces that are snowyCozy, calm feelingsCotton-ball snowman
Week 2
Winter Animals		Move like a bear, penguin, fox“Animals in winter” chartCount & sort animalsHibernate, migrate, adaptHow we care for animals in coldGentle with living thingsHandprint penguin
Week 3
Staying Warm & Cozy		Dress-for-winter relayName winter clothes (D: down, dry)Match mittens (pairs)How clothes keep us warmPeople who help in winterCozy calm-down timeDesign a mitten
Week 4
Winter Fun		Indoor “snowball” tossTell about winter playGraph favorite winter gamesWhy we see our breathWinter fun around the worldShare the fun; take turnsSnowflake painting
FLORIDA EARLY LEARNING STANDARDS — DOMAINS ADDRESSED
Physical DevelopmentApproaches to LearningSocial & Emotional DevelopmentLanguage & LiteracyMathematical ThinkingScientific InquirySocial StudiesCreative Expression
Milestones this band builds toward: writing their name & knowing many letter-sounds; counting to 20 & making patterns; retelling stories with emergent writing; solving problems and cooperating in groups; and self-regulating — VPK / kindergarten ready.
Aligned to the Florida Early Learning and Developmental Standards: Birth to Kindergarten (2017), FDOE Division of Early Learning. Domain alignments are paraphrased teaching summaries, not the official standards text. See the standards by age in our Milestone Wizard →

Bear Phonics

  • Warm-up: Sound Clock review, then new D. Teach: read “Feed Me” (Lesson 5).
  • Workbook: Bear Tracks Lesson 5 — Meet D, Write D.
  • Apply: re-read the decodable; Friday mastery check + “I did it!”.
  • Watch Lesson 5 free on Bear Phonics →

Your Feelings Matter

  • Feelings check-in every morning.
  • Name feelings + causes; role-play helping.
  • Get the book →

  • Bear Phonics “Feed Me” decodable reader. Watch on Bear Phonics →

Week · Sub-themeFocusActivity
Week 1
Snow & Ice		Winter STEMBuild & test a “melt the ice” experiment
Week 2
Winter Animals		Winter animalsResearch how animals survive winter
Week 3
Staying Warm & Cozy		EngineeringDesign the tallest “snow” tower
Week 4
Winter Fun		Winter artsWinter journaling & photography

Approaches to LearningSocial & Emotional DevelopmentLanguage & LiteracyMathematical ThinkingScientific InquirySocial StudiesCreative Expression

January · Infant

Winter Wonders · a note to take home

Brrr — winter wonders! Bundle up and explore snow, ice, and cozy stories. Cold-weather play is great for growing bodies and minds.

Letters D · P · QNumber 6Shape: diamondColor: blueTheme: Winter Wonders

Try this at home

  • A snowflake cut-out craft.
  • A “winter animals” matching card.
  • A cozy bedtime-reading tip.
  • D / P / Q + number-6 tracing.

Sing together

  • “Snowflake, Snowflake”
  • “I’m a Little Snowman”

Read together

Snuggle up and share a read-aloud together — try Your Feelings Matter or a favorite picture book. Decodable Bear Phonics readers begin at age three.

February · Infant

Kindness & Friendship  ·  Letters R · U · V
MONTH February
THEME Kindness & Friendship
LETTERS R · U · V
Number 7 · Shape heart · Color pink
Teacher: _______________Classroom: _______________Week of: _______________Take-home: The Home Den family pack

Focus — sensory play, gentle movement, and one new sound

Sound & Sensory

  • Lots of gentle “I love you” faces.
  • Bear Phonics /r/ sound at play.
  • Soft heart pillows.

Songs & Lap Play

  • “Skidamarink”
  • “You Are My Sunshine”
  • Cuddle songs

Sensory Picks

  • Soft heart toys
  • Feelings-face cards
  • Mirror
  • Red / pink soft fabrics
FLORIDA EARLY LEARNING STANDARDS — DOMAINS ADDRESSED
Physical DevelopmentApproaches to LearningSocial & Emotional DevelopmentLanguage & LiteracyScientific InquiryCreative Expression
Milestones this band builds toward: secure attachment & trust; exploring with the senses and reaching, grasping & grabbing; responding to voices, babbling & first sounds; and gaining head, trunk & hand control.
Aligned to the Florida Early Learning and Developmental Standards: Birth to Kindergarten (2017), FDOE Division of Early Learning. Domain alignments are paraphrased teaching summaries, not the official standards text. See the standards by age in our Milestone Wizard →

Bear Phonics

  • Play the Bear Phonics Alphabet Anthem from Mrs. Bear’s Welcome to Success! album — the ABCs in a song. Play on YouTube →

Your Feelings Matter

  • A laminated feelings-faces card nearby — name your own face: “Teacher feels happy!”
  • Get the Your Feelings Matter book →

Books & Read-Alouds

  • Your Feelings Matter by Mrs. Bear — name feelings together. Get on Amazon →
  • Have You Filled a Bucket Today? by Carol McCloud
  • Should I Share My Ice Cream? by Mo Willems
Browse the Reading Library →

Character Development — Kindness & Friendship

  • Use gentle hands and kind words.
  • Give a friend a high-five or a hug.

ECE Fun Fact — for teachers

Kindness is contagious and measurable — kids who see peers helping are more likely to help. Narrate kindness out loud: “Look how Maria shared!”

Weekly Plan — four sub-themes across the developmental domains

Week · Sub-themePhysicalLanguage / LiteracySocial-EmotionalSensory / Explore
Week 1
What Is a Friend?		Mirror-a-friend movement“A friend is someone who…”Make & greet a friendPartner play-dough hearts
Week 2
Kind Words & Deeds		Deliver-a-kindness relayKind words practice (R: respect)Fill a bucket, not dip itRed / pink sensory rice
Week 3
Working Together		Cooperative parachute play“We can do it together”Solve a problem with a friendShared building bin
Week 4
Hearts & Helpers		Helper-of-the-day movement jobsThank-you words for helpersShow love & appreciationHeart-shaped sensory bin

Week 1
What Is a Friend?		Mirror-a-friend movement“A friend is someone who…”Count our friendsMake & greet a friendFriendship portrait
Week 2
Kind Words & Deeds		Deliver-a-kindness relayKind words practice (R: respect)Count kind acts on our jarFill a bucket, not dip itKindness-heart craft
Week 3
Working Together		Cooperative parachute play“We can do it together”Build a tower as a team; count blocksSolve a problem with a friendGroup mural
Week 4
Hearts & Helpers		Helper-of-the-day movement jobsThank-you words for helpersCount & sort heartsShow love & appreciationValentines for friends
FLORIDA EARLY LEARNING STANDARDS — DOMAINS ADDRESSED
Physical DevelopmentApproaches to LearningLanguage & LiteracyMathematical ThinkingScientific InquirySocial & Emotional DevelopmentCreative Expression
Milestones this band builds toward: running, jumping & scribbling; speaking in 2–3 word phrases; sorting & matching by one attribute; symbolic and parallel play; and growing self-help skills.
Aligned to the Florida Early Learning and Developmental Standards: Birth to Kindergarten (2017), FDOE Division of Early Learning. Domain alignments are paraphrased teaching summaries, not the official standards text. See the standards by age in our Milestone Wizard →

Character Development — Kindness & Friendship

  • Use gentle hands and kind words.
  • Give a friend a high-five or a hug.

ECE Fun Fact — for teachers

Kindness is contagious and measurable — kids who see peers helping are more likely to help. Narrate kindness out loud: “Look how Maria shared!”

Bear Phonics

  • Warm-up: Sound Clock review, then new R. Teach: read “The Deer Sees Seeds” (Lesson 6).
  • Workbook: Bear Tracks Lesson 6 — Meet R, Write R.
  • Apply: re-read the decodable; Friday mastery check + “I did it!”.
  • Watch Lesson 6 free on Bear Phonics →

  • Feelings check-in every morning.
  • Name feelings + causes; role-play helping.

Kindness & Friendship · a note to take home

Kindness and friendship are our focus. Notice and name kind acts at home — “that was so kind!” Kids repeat what we celebrate.

March · Infant

Things That Grow  ·  Letters I · X · Z
MONTH March
THEME Things That Grow
LETTERS I · X · Z
Number 8 · Shape oval · Color purple
Teacher: _______________Classroom: _______________Week of: _______________Take-home: The Home Den family pack

Focus — sensory play, gentle movement, and one new sound

Sound & Sensory

  • Touch a leaf or a safe soft plant.
  • Bear Phonics long-I “iii” sound.
  • Grass / soil texture board (supervised).

Songs & Lap Play

  • “The Green Grass Grew All Around”
  • “You Are My Sunshine”
  • Gentle growing songs

Sensory Picks

  • Safe plant textures
  • Baby-animal soft toys
  • Mirror
  • Green soft fabrics
FLORIDA EARLY LEARNING STANDARDS — DOMAINS ADDRESSED
Physical DevelopmentApproaches to LearningSocial & Emotional DevelopmentLanguage & LiteracyScientific InquiryCreative Expression
Milestones this band builds toward: secure attachment & trust; exploring with the senses and reaching, grasping & grabbing; responding to voices, babbling & first sounds; and gaining head, trunk & hand control.
Aligned to the Florida Early Learning and Developmental Standards: Birth to Kindergarten (2017), FDOE Division of Early Learning. Domain alignments are paraphrased teaching summaries, not the official standards text. See the standards by age in our Milestone Wizard →

Bear Phonics

  • Play the Bear Phonics Alphabet Anthem from Mrs. Bear’s Welcome to Success! album — the ABCs in a song. Play on YouTube →

Your Feelings Matter

  • A laminated feelings-faces card nearby — name your own face: “Teacher feels happy!”
  • Get the Your Feelings Matter book →

Books & Read-Alouds

  • Your Feelings Matter by Mrs. Bear — name feelings together. Get on Amazon →
  • The Tiny Seed by Eric Carle
  • Planting a Rainbow by Lois Ehlert
Browse the Reading Library →

Character Development — Patience

  • Wait for a turn with a sand timer.
  • Watch our seed grow — good things take time.

ECE Fun Fact — for teachers

Watching a seed sprout teaches patience and cause-and-effect like nothing else. Plant something — the wait is the lesson.

MONTH March
THEME Things That Grow
LETTERS I · X · Z
Number 8 · Shape oval · Color purple
Teacher: _______________Classroom: _______________Week of: _______________Take-home: The Home Den family pack

Weekly Plan — four sub-themes across the developmental domains

Week · Sub-themePhysicalLanguage / LiteracySocial-EmotionalSensory / Explore
Week 1
Seeds & Plants		Grow from seed to tree (movement)Plant words: seed, root, stem, leafPatience: good things take timeSoil & seed digging bin
Week 2
In the Garden		Dig, rake, water (pretend)Label a garden pictureCare for our class plantFlower & petal sensory bin
Week 3
Baby Animals		Move like baby animalsMatch animals to babiesGentle & nurturingFarm small-world bin
Week 4
Growing Me		Measure how tall I am“When I was a baby / now”“I am growing & capable”Measuring & height play
FLORIDA EARLY LEARNING STANDARDS — DOMAINS ADDRESSED
Physical DevelopmentApproaches to LearningSocial & Emotional DevelopmentLanguage & LiteracyScientific InquiryCreative Expression
Milestones this band builds toward: walking, climbing & using first words and gestures; imitating and beginning to pretend; following simple one-step directions; and noticing self and others.

April · Infant

Our Big Blue Earth  ·  Letters Y (+ review)
MONTH April
THEME Our Big Blue Earth
LETTERS Y (+ review)
Number 9 · Shape crescent · Color teal
Teacher: _______________Classroom: _______________Week of: _______________Take-home: The Home Den family pack

Focus — sensory play, gentle movement, and one new sound

Sound & Sensory

  • Feel water and grass (supervised).
  • Bear Phonics /y/ long-I sound.
  • Nature texture board.

Songs & Lap Play

  • “The Earth Is Our Home”
  • “You Are My Sunshine”
  • Gentle nature songs

Sensory Picks

  • Water / sponge play (close supervision)
  • Earth-ball soft toy
  • Mirror
  • Blue / green fabrics

Physical DevelopmentApproaches to LearningSocial & Emotional DevelopmentLanguage & LiteracyScientific InquiryCreative Expression
Milestones this band builds toward: secure attachment & trust; exploring with the senses and reaching, grasping & grabbing; responding to voices, babbling & first sounds; and gaining head, trunk & hand control.

Character Development — Stewardship

  • Turn off the water; pick up one piece of litter.
  • “We take care of our Earth.”

ECE Fun Fact — for teachers

Young children are natural environmentalists. Simple habits — turning off lights, sorting recycling — form a lifelong “green” identity when started early.

May · Infant

On the Move  ·  Letters Review A–Z
MONTH May
THEME On the Move
LETTERS Review A–Z
Number 10 · Shape pentagon · Color rainbow
Teacher: _______________Classroom: _______________Week of: _______________Take-home: The Home Den family pack

Focus — sensory play, gentle movement, and one new sound

Sound & Sensory

  • Gentle rides in arms — moving is fun!
  • Bear Phonics igh long-I sound.
  • Roll and reach movement play.

Songs & Lap Play

  • “Row, Row, Row Your Boat”
  • “The Wheels on the Bus”
  • Bouncing lap songs

Sensory Picks

  • Soft vehicle toys
  • Textured balls
  • Mirror
  • Scarves to reach for

Physical DevelopmentApproaches to LearningSocial & Emotional DevelopmentLanguage & LiteracyScientific InquiryCreative Expression
Milestones this band builds toward: secure attachment & trust; exploring with the senses and reaching, grasping & grabbing; responding to voices, babbling & first sounds; and gaining head, trunk & hand control.
Aligned to the Florida Early Learning and Developmental Standards: Birth to Kindergarten (2017), FDOE Division of Early Learning. Domain alignments are paraphrased teaching summaries, not the official standards text. See the standards by age in our Milestone Wizard →

Character Development — Confidence & Courage

  • Try a new big move — “I did it!”
  • Clap for brave tries.

ECE Fun Fact — for teachers

Big-muscle movement wires the brain for learning. Crossing the midline (reaching across the body) actually strengthens reading readiness. Get them moving!

The Home Den — the family take-home pack

Goes in every backpack this month.

  • A “things that go” sorting page.
  • A family movement-game card.
  • A “how I get to school” map.
  • Number-10 + alphabet review sheet.

Infants get the take-home pack + a sensory focus instead of a weekly grid.

The printable Home Den pack for this month — mini-book, practice pages & cover sheet — is available to The Buzz monthly subscribers.

Join The Buzz →

Snuggle up and share a read-aloud — try Your Feelings Matter or a favorite picture book.

Teacher Resources — May (all ages)

Book list: Bear Phonics Light, Right, High (Block I) (watch on Bear Phonics) · a favorite on the move picture book (teacher’s choice) · Your Feelings Matter (get on Amazon).

Letters this month: Review A–Z · Number 10 · pentagon · rainbow.

Materials shopping list — tap any item to shop on Amazon: Toy vehicles · ramps · a class map · number-10 ten-frames · scarves for movement.

Printables: themed activity pages · letter & number practice · the May Home Den cover sheet · “See the Work” Friday checklist.

Week · Sub-themePhysicalLanguage / LiteracyMath / ScienceSocial-EmotionalCreative

Things That Go		Move like different vehiclesVehicle words & soundsCount & sort vehiclesWait & take turns “driving”Build a vehicle

Bear Phonics

  • Sound Clock review, then new igh; read “Light, Right, High.”
  • “I do / we do / you do” — trace the igh row (Bear Tracks).
  • Friday recite + “I did it!” Watch Block I free on Bear Phonics →

Your Feelings Matter

  • Daily feelings check-in chart.
  • Grow the class kindness tree.
  • Get the book →

  • Freight Train by Donald Crews

On the Move  ·  Letters Review A–Z
MONTH May
THEME On the Move
LETTERS Review A–Z
Number 10 · Shape pentagon · Color rainbow
Teacher: _______________Classroom: _______________Week of: _______________Take-home: The Home Den family pack

The lead band. The Marva-rhythm daily block folds Bear Phonics in as the literacy core.

Weekly Plan — four sub-themes across the developmental domains

Week · Sub-themePhysicalLanguage & LiteracyMathScienceSocial StudiesSocial-EmotionalCreative
Week 1
Things That Go		Move like different vehiclesVehicle words & soundsCount & sort vehiclesWheels & how things rollVehicles that help usWait & take turns “driving”Build a vehicle
Week 2
On Land		Cars, trains, bikes movementRetell a tripFast & slow; near & farRamps: steeper = fasterRoads, rails & signsSafety & following rulesRoad / track collage
Week 3
On Water & Air		Row a boat; fly a plane (movement)Water & air travel wordsFloat & sink; count boatsWhat floats? What flies?Boats & planes take us farBrave to try new thingsPaper boat / plane
Week 4
How I Move		Run, jump, spin, balance stationsAction words (verbs)Count jumps; graph our movesMuscles help me moveHow I get to schoolConfidence: “I can move!”Dance-and-paint movement art
FLORIDA EARLY LEARNING STANDARDS — DOMAINS ADDRESSED
Physical DevelopmentApproaches to LearningSocial & Emotional DevelopmentLanguage & LiteracyMathematical ThinkingScientific InquirySocial StudiesCreative Expression
Milestones this band builds toward: writing their name & knowing many letter-sounds; counting to 20 & making patterns; retelling stories with emergent writing; solving problems and cooperating in groups; and self-regulating — VPK / kindergarten ready.
Aligned to the Florida Early Learning and Developmental Standards: Birth to Kindergarten (2017), FDOE Division of Early Learning. Domain alignments are paraphrased teaching summaries, not the official standards text. See the standards by age in our Milestone Wizard →

Bear Phonics

  • Warm-up: Sound Clock review, then new igh. Teach: read “Light, Right, High” (Block I).
  • Workbook: Bear Tracks Block I — Meet igh, Write igh.
  • Apply: re-read the decodable; Friday mastery check + “I did it!”.
  • Watch Block I free on Bear Phonics →

Your Feelings Matter

  • Feelings check-in every morning.
  • Name feelings + causes; role-play helping.
  • Get the book →

Books & Read-Alouds

  • Your Feelings Matter. Get on Amazon →
  • Bear Phonics “Light, Right, High” decodable reader. Watch on Bear Phonics →
  • Freight Train by Donald Crews
  • Little Blue Truck by Alice Schertle
Browse the Reading Library →

Character Development — Confidence & Courage

  • “Brave means trying even when it’s tricky.”
  • Share a goal out loud with friends.

May · Infant

On the Move · a note to take home

We’re on the move! Explore things that go and all the ways bodies move. Big-muscle play builds brains — get moving together.

Letters Review A–ZNumber 10Shape: pentagonColor: rainbowTheme: On the Move

Try this at home

  • A “things that go” sorting page.
  • A family movement-game card.
  • A “how I get to school” map.
  • Number-10 + alphabet review sheet.

Sing together

  • “The Wheels on the Bus”
  • “Row, Row, Row Your Boat”

Read together

Snuggle up and share a read-aloud together — try Your Feelings Matter or a favorite picture book. Decodable Bear Phonics readers begin at age three.

Physical DevelopmentApproaches to LearningSocial & Emotional DevelopmentLanguage & LiteracyScientific InquiryCreative Expression

Pretend play is the highest form of early learning. When children act out stories, they build vocabulary, self-regulation, and problem-solving. Protect playtime fiercely!

The Home Den — the family take-home pack

Goes in every backpack this month.

  • A “make your own story” fold-book.
  • A dress-up / pretend prompt card.
  • An open-ended art invitation.
  • A “dream big” drawing page.

The printable Home Den pack for this month — mini-book, practice pages & cover sheet — is available to The Buzz monthly subscribers.

Join The Buzz →

Then read this month’s Bear Phonics book together: The Deer Sees Seeds.

Songs & Fingerplays

  • “If You’re Happy and You Know It”
  • “The Wheels on the Bus”
  • “Twinkle, Twinkle” (imagine the star)

Materials — tap to shop

Dress-up clothes · puppets · open-ended art supplies · blocks · story stones · musical instruments.

Shop the Center Bundles →

Teacher Resources — July (all ages)

Book list: Bear Phonics The Deer Sees Seeds (Block 2 review) (Lesson 6) (watch on Bear Phonics) · a favorite imagination station picture book (teacher’s choice) · Your Feelings Matter (get on Amazon).

Letters this month: Review A–Z · Number 12 · review · purple.

Materials shopping list — tap any item to shop on Amazon: Dress-up clothes · puppets · open-ended art supplies · blocks · story stones · musical instruments.

Printables: themed activity pages · letter & number practice · the July Home Den cover sheet · “See the Work” Friday checklist.

The Home Den 🐾 Family Handout

July · Infant

Imagination Station · a note to take home

Welcome to the Imagination Station! Pretend play is powerful learning. Make up stories, build blanket forts, and dream big together.

Letters Review A–ZNumber 12Shape: reviewColor: purpleTheme: Imagination Station

Try this at home

  • A “make your own story” fold-book.
  • A dress-up / pretend prompt card.
  • An open-ended art invitation.
  • A “dream big” drawing page.

Sing together

  • “If You’re Happy and You Know It”
  • “The Wheels on the Bus”

Read together

Snuggle up and share a read-aloud together — try Your Feelings Matter or a favorite picture book. Decodable Bear Phonics readers begin at age three.

Please note: The Lesson Plan Wizard is a free teaching resource. Every theme, activity, song, and printable is an original work by Mrs. Bear. Domain alignments are teacher-friendly summaries drawn from the Florida Early Learning and Developmental Standards: Birth to Kindergarten (2017) — not the official standards text, and not a diagnostic tool. Children develop at their own pace.

Bear Phonics videos and the Your Feelings Matter books are available separately — every plan is free to use, no strings. As an Amazon Associate, The Preschool Professional earns from qualifying purchases.
